LIVE: President and CEO of Qualcomm Cristiano Amon Addresses India AI summit | N18L

Firstpost(9.3M) ·55:21 ·1.8K views · 2026-02-20
Cristiano Amon (President and CEO, Qualcomm)
AI is transitioning from a tool we occasionally utilize to a pervasive "agent" integrated into every device and network, fundamentally shifting the human-computer interface and positioning India to lead the next global era of industrialization and digital services.
TL;DR AI is transitioning from a tool we occasionally utilize to a pervasive "agent" integrated into every device and network, fundamentally shifting the human-computer interface and positioning India to lead the next global era of industrialization and digital services. ...

TL;DR

AI is transitioning from a tool we occasionally utilize to a pervasive "agent" integrated into every device and network, fundamentally shifting the human-computer interface and positioning India to lead the next global era of industrialization and digital services.

The Shift from Chatbots to Pervasive Agents

  • Redefining the Interface: AI is moving beyond keyboards and touchscreens to systems that understand what humans see, hear, say, and write.
  • The "Agent" Centrality: In the mobile ecosystem, traditional operating systems and application stores will be superseded by AI agents.
      • Autonomy: These agents will understand human intentions, making decisions and executing tasks across the internet and local hardware without being bound by specific software constructs.
      • Cross-Device Experience: While smartphones currently center our digital lives, agents will become accessible through a variety of hardware, including smart glasses, pendants, and wearables.
  • Contextual Relevance: For agents to be effective, they must be contextually aware, processing massive amounts of personal data locally to remain fast, relevant, and private.

Hardware Evolution and Hybrid AI Processing

  • Cloud-Edge Synergy: Amon argues that the debate between "cloud vs. edge" is misplaced; the future is a seamless, distributed model.
      • Device-Level Tasks: Critical functions requiring instant response or personal context will run on-device.
      • Cloud-Level Tasks: High-compute, non-sensitive workloads will remain in the cloud.
  • New Form Factors:
      • Smart Glasses: Predicted to proliferate by the end of this year, these devices will allow "look-and-buy" commerce.
      • Example: A user could look at a product and tell their glasses to "check this on Flipkart and buy it," integrating camera vision with payment systems.
  • Qualcomm’s Scalability: The company is developing chips ranging from milliwatts for earbuds to 2,000-watt processors for data centers to support this ubiquitous intelligence.

6G: The Network as a Sensing Platform

  • Beyond Connectivity: While 5G focused on broadband data, 6G will integrate AI into the very fabric of the telecom network.
  • Sensing at Scale: A major feature of 6G is its role as a "sensing network," utilizing radar-like techniques to map environments.
      • Industrial Use Cases: This sensing capability will support autonomous driving, drone traffic management, and aerial economy control.
      • Context Provider: The network itself will provide vital environmental context to individual AI agents, enhancing their utility.

Strategic Opportunities for India

  • Digital Leapfrogging: Just as India leapfrogged fixed-line internet to become a mobile-first economy, it is now positioned to lead in AI-driven services.
  • Key Growth Sectors:
      • Smart Manufacturing: India’s rise as a global manufacturing hub will be accelerated by smart automation and "physical AI."
      • Social Infrastructure: AI will increase the scale and reach of healthcare, provide ongoing personalized learning in education, and modernize agriculture.
  • Data Consumption: India already has some of the highest mobile data consumption rates globally, providing a massive foundation for training and deploying large-scale AI models.
"Intelligence is now shifting from something we utilize to something that's simply all around us, everywhere, all the time." — Cristiano Amon
"The smartphone today is at the center of everything that we do. But now that's going to get replaced by an agent... you're no longer bound by constructs of your hardware or OS." — Cristiano Amon
"6G is going to be... as big as going from voice to data, and it's all part of this future of AI." — Cristiano Amon
Happen with AI in general, what I'd like to talk to you today is about the next chapter of AI. And this is something that's very near and dear to Qualcomm. We've been—we've been talking about this because I think we're really entering now the next phase of AI. As AI gets developed, it's going to be part of everything that we do, and especially the interaction that we have with computers and with digital systems. So intelligence is now shifting from something we utilize to something that's simply all around us, everywhere, all the time, especially with the devices. I actually love the presentation right before from my friend Jitu from Cisco when he talked about the traffic change from chatbots to agents. And this is important. I'm, you know, I've been often talking about this, how we should be thinking about AI in a much broader sense. It's easier for a company like Qualcomm to talk about this because we build a lot of the chips that go into devices where the humans are. So as you create AI in the data center and you train and create those models, all this data, and you deploy this, you start to see that this gets utilized in different ways. One fundamental thing that AI is doing for us is changing the human-computer interface because we now have to learn how to use a computer. If, you know, I've been often talking about this in different presentations, we had to learn how to use an AS2 keyboard and we still use that on a laptop, then we used to touch a screen. But now the AI understands what we see, what we hear, what we say, and what we write. So in itself, it's changing computers; it's changing the devices we interact with and it's becoming a pervasive technology that is going to be everywhere. And I think that's the mission of Qualcomm. When I think about what we are going to do, it is the same way that what we did with mobile communications and the creation of the computer that fits in the palm of your hand—this ability to take that intelligence everywhere. And it's going to be creating a number of important shifts in the industry. I want to start talking about the mobile industry. We may have had the privilege as a company to be part of every single transition of wireless technologies. And today, I'm going to talk about the next one that is coming as well. What we saw with the transition of wireless technology is that fundamentally, at every generation of wireless, you saw big shifts, not only in devices but in companies. Because of the transition, for example, when you went to the ability to have a phone that you carry with you all the way to connecting the phone to the internet, things changed. All of a sudden, that phone became a computer and it started to drive the future of the internet. Like a country like India that leapfrogged, I think, the internet and went straight to the mobile internet. And that's going to be true again when you think about AI. For example, in the mobile ecosystem, AI is going to fundamentally change how we think about the mobile device. All of you today, and me included, I think we look at our smartphone as our inseparable device where most of our digital life is. And the smartphone today is at the center of everything that we do. But now, that's going to get replaced by an agent. When you think about the entire value chain that got created, for example, for the mobile industry, there's an enormous amount of value in things like OSs and application stores. And that becomes like the platform when you're going to develop an application that you're going to do different things into. An agent now understands human intentions because, you know, you just need to tell him what you want, or he's going to see what you see and make a decision for you, assuming you authorize it. When that happens, that's where the value is because then the agent is free. It can go to the internet and do things, it can go to your phone and do things, and you're no longer bound by constructs of your hardware or OS and the application. So as a result, we expect that AI is going to have a fundamental shift in the mobile industry where the agent is going to be at the very center. And as the agent is at the very center, everything surrounds the agent. You can access the agent from your mobile phone, but you can also access the agent from your glasses or from a pendant or from anything that you wear. I think we're going to look at the mobile ecosystem right now not only as a single device experience, but you're going to connect to agents across multiple types of devices. And I think this is incredibly exciting. And that's not only unique to what you're going to see in consumers; that's going to happen also with things. You can now also create AI that's going to get trained on different things—on physical signals like physical AI, on sensor data—and you're going to deploy that in every computer. So what's exciting about AI is it's going to very quickly evolve from something where you go to a browser and you ask a question. And I think, as my colleague from Cisco said, it's got trained on all the publicly available data on the internet. You're now going to go to a different type of AI experience that's going to be the fundamental software that is going to run in all the devices around us and how you're going to have interaction on those devices. So I also want to basically, as we think about this future, I just want to give you an example. What we saw across the industry is workloads or use cases have shifted. Devices didn't go anywhere, but their workload shifted. We used to do a lot of things in the early days of the internet on your laptop. And for example, e-commerce: you would do it on your laptop. Now most of the e-commerce in the world is done on a phone. Tomorrow—or it could be as early as within the end of this year as you start to see the proliferation of glasses—if you have a glass that has agents, it's connected to the internet and has a camera, the glass sees what you see. You can just look at something and say, "I'd like to buy this." What is it? "Can you check this, for example, check this on Flipkart, and just buy it for me? I'd like to buy this." With the integration of payment systems, you get a bill and say, "Pay this, notify me when I'm done," and so forth. So I think we're going to see this fundamental change of devices. But that's also going to be true about the revolution that's happening on robotics and the revolution that is actually happening on industrial. So that's an incredible opportunity, and we have been incredibly focused as a company to basically drive that future of computing. There's also a big debate, which I believe is the wrong way to look into it, which is about cloud and edge. There's a lot of debate about, "Oh, this is going to be running on the cloud," or "This is going to be running on the edge." And it actually does not matter. I want to think about your device today. Your smartphone today has an incredible amount of processing power, and there are a number of different things that run in our smartphone. If you put it on airplane mode, you probably don't use it. You just put it back and wait until you get connectivity again. It's the most cloud-connected device because those things work as one. It is, and you're going to have now intelligence that's going to be incredibly distributed across the cloud, across the near edge, the network in itself, and on-device. And it's all going to work seamlessly. There are going to be things that you're going to be able to do on the device because they require an instant response, or it requires unique context, requiring unique information that is relevant to you. Something else is going to be done on the cloud, and they're both going to be growing and transforming how we think about computers. So I'd like to provide a simple description. Let's say we are all using agents, and you're going to pick the agent that you like. For the agent to be useful, it needs to be fast and it needs to be relevant for you. Let's go back to the example I provided on the glasses. And you have those smart glasses and you're walking around and you have a camera, then all of a sudden you see somebody and you ask this glass, like it's a friend next to you, "Who is this person?" And you want to get a response. "This is so and so." Or you're going to say, "Can you translate this for me? What is this? Can you pay this for me?" You want this thing to be seamless, with no friction. So certain things are going to be done on your device and other things are going to be on the cloud; it's going to be completely transparent to you. But the interesting thing is those agents, for them to be very useful, they need to be contextually aware of what is relevant to you. So over time, the agent that I'm going to be using and the agent that you're going to be using—they need to be relevant to me. So you're going to have a lot of things that are going to be processed and understood about you. So much so that I believe that in the endgame—I think it was said in the prior presentation from Cisco—all this available data that is publicly on the internet that you train models with is a fraction of the data that is going to be generated. If you have, for example, a glass with a camera that sees everything that you see, it tries to annotate that image, get information about the image and the context, reads what you read, and so forth. That is an incredible amount of data, and that's going to be providing a lot of important context for those models to be relevant to you. That is the future, and it's an incredible transformation. It's going to transform every industry. No industry is immune to this, and I think what we are doing as Qualcomm is really creating the future hardware and software that will help enable this future across all the devices. We were a very unique semiconductor company. I think we're probably one of the few companies that can be working on chips from sub-milliwatts for a smart earbud that you're going to wear, all the way to now 2,000 watts for a chip on the data center. But I think that's the incredible future: that AI is going to transform every single computer and the agents are going to be at the center of the experience. It's going to replace a lot of the OSs and application definitions we see today. And I think that that is the new future of technology, including the future of mobility. And that's why I am incredibly excited about this. And with that, I want to talk about something that is happening which is about the next generation of wireless technologies. I would like to provide an example from the past. When you think about telecom networks—and I think we're probably one of the, you know, American telecom companies that are really focused on the evolution of cellular technology—when you think about the evolution of this sector, it all started with providing a telephone. I think for all of us, it was an incredible thing. You have a twisted copper pair that gets to your home, you pick up, you get a dial tone, you dial, and eventually, you could dial anybody in the world with a telephone. Even how cellular started was about making sure all of us had the ability to carry a telephone. That was 2G, where you can call everyone. That's different today. Now you have a very high-performance broadband network for data. Voice is just one application among many applications that you do at the network. It fundamentally changed the nature of the infrastructure; the equipment was different, the use cases were different. We're heading to the next big transformation of the telecom sector. 6G is going to provide an evolution of connectivity: faster speed, lower latency, higher coverage. But that's not the story. That's just a piece of the story. This just continues to improve the connectivity. The bigger part of 6G is AI. Like I said before, it is now going to come to the telecom network. And that becomes a large-scale AI network that is processing and getting trained on all of the signals that happen at the network and providing new capabilities. One of the biggest features of 6G is that the network is a sensing network at scale. I'm going to give an example. The network not only will provide connectivity between your device and the internet but will sense everything that's around you. It will use techniques that you see today in autonomous driving cars, like radars as an example, to detect your environment. And it's going to provide a map of everything that is happening at scale. And you're going to have completely different types of services for different industries. It will provide context for your agents, which is very important, and the network will have that role. It will provide traffic management systems in some of the use cases that are going to be part of full self-driving cars. It will do drone detection and manage the traffic control of the economy that's going to be aerial in the wide area network, and much more, because AI is also going to the network. It's going to be one of the biggest transitions I think we've had, as big as going from voice to data, and it's all part of this future of AI. And I just want now to make another parallel to the presentation from my colleague from Cisco. It puts a fine point on the network that needs to be built, the capability of the infrastructure, the security, and the trust. But that is an incredible future with technology. And as I get to the end of the presentation, I want to highlight that India has an incredible opportunity with this transformation. We have seen that those big shifts in technology create opportunity, change players, and change the role of different countries as they provide a global scale for the technology. And that's an incredible opportunity for India. I look at what happened in mobile in India, and one of the largest data consumption rates per user in mobile devices in the world is in India. The whole internet is mobile. When you think about the potential of all those things that I just discussed—about how AI is going to change everything, creating new devices, new experiences, new services—that becomes a massive opportunity. And when I look at the ambitions that were set by the AI summit, I'm going to provide just some examples. Those are just examples. It can be much broader, but I just want to connect with some of the ambitions of the summit. There is a process of jumping into large-scale industrialization. India is becoming a global manufacturing hub as well, and with AI, you go from the very beginning with smart manufacturing and automation. The incredible change that is happening in this sector is enabled by those technologies. Same thing with smart cities and the ability to continue to evolve the infrastructure. There is the ability to use AI to increase the scale, the reach, and the access for healthcare. Consider how you change education. Those are incredibly powerful learning tools—the ability to actually use some of those technologies to empower people with information. And you're going to have an ongoing learning experience. Think about those agents that are with you all the time, answering questions, telling you how to do things, especially when you think in the context, for example, of those new devices such as smart glasses. And it can fundamentally change industries, for example, such as agriculture. And these are just a few examples of the potential of connecting this technology with everything I think that is going on in India. It's an incredible and exciting future enabled by AI, and it's really going to be about meeting the ambition of democratizing this technology for everyone and actually having an important role in increasing the global welfare. And you know, as a company that has always been focused on enabling our partners in other industries to innovate, I think the history of Qualcomm is that we never believe it is the job of one company to be responsible for all the innovation. It's really to enable many industries and partners. We're incredibly excited to play a very small part in this mission. Thank you very much for the opportunity to talk to all of you, and enjoy the rest of the summit. Thank you.
